## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics / nonlinear dynamics (nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly explicit time t, which is the standard state-space form of (possibly forced/damped) nonlinear harmonic oscillator models. Typical structures include linear restoring forces, nonlinear stiffness from an anharmonic potential, linear/nonlinear damping, self-excitation, and periodic forcing or parameter modulation.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear undamped oscillator (Hooke restoring): dv_dt = -c0 * x (small-amplitude mass-spring motion)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (damped harmonic oscillator)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring, nonlinear resonance)
- Quintic stiffness extension: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 - c3 * v (strongly anharmonic restoring force)
- Pendulum small-to-large angle restoring: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (rotational oscillator with geometric nonlinearity)
- Nonlinear (quadratic) drag damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (high-Re drag / amplitude-dependent damping)
- Coulomb (dry) friction damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * (v / (Abs(v) + c3)) (stick-slip-like friction; smoothed sign(v))
- Van der Pol self-excited oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (negative damping at small |x|, limit cycle formation)
- Rayleigh oscillator (nonlinear damping in v): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - v**2) * v (self-excitation via velocity-dependent damping)
- Externally forced oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t + c4) (periodic driving force)
- Forced Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t + c5) (nonlinear resonance/chaos regimes)
- Parametrically excited (Mathieu-type) oscillator: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t + c3)) * x - c4 * v (time-varying stiffness, parametric resonance)
- Potential-gradient form (conservative + damping): dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) - c3 * v (motion in polynomial potential with dissipation)
- Nonlinear coupling (state-dependent frequency/damping): dv_dt = -c0 * x * (c1 + c2 * x**2) - c3 * v * (c4 + c5 * x**2) (amplitude-dependent stiffness and damping)
- Jerk/servo-like feedback term (explicit time modulation of damping): dv_dt = -c0 * x - (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) * v (periodically modulated dissipation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring force only → dv_dt depends primarily on x (often an odd function of x), indicating an underlying potential U(x) with dv_dt = -dU/dx.
- Anharmonic stiffness → appearance of x**3, x**5, or sin(c*x) terms; these create amplitude-dependent frequency and can yield bistability (Duffing).
- Viscous dissipation → linear -c*v term; causes exponential decay of oscillation amplitude and phase-space spiraling to equilibrium.
- High-speed drag → -c*v*Abs(v) (or higher powers of v); produces stronger damping at large speeds and non-exponential amplitude decay.
- Dry friction / stick-slip → sign-like dependence on v (often implemented as v/(Abs(v)+c)); creates non-smooth dynamics and can yield finite-time stopping.
- Self-excited limit cycles → negative damping at small amplitude (e.g., (c - x**2)*v or (c - v**2)*v), balancing positive damping at large amplitude.
- External periodic forcing → additive sin/cos(c*t) term; yields entrainment, resonance peaks, and possibly quasiperiodicity/chaos with nonlinearity.
- Parametric excitation → time-periodic coefficient multiplying x (e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x); can generate instability tongues and subharmonic responses.
- Symmetry cues → odd restoring terms (x, x**3) preserve x→-x symmetry; even terms (x**2, x**4) indicate bias/asymmetry or shifted equilibrium.
- State-dependent damping/stiffness → products like x**2*v or x*v indicate amplitude-dependent energy loss or geometric/constitutive nonlinear coupling.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO4)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - omega0**c1*(gamma*Abs(v)**c2 + c3)*x - omega0**c4*x
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed) simplifies structurally to
\[
F(t,x,v)=A\sin t\;+\;B\,v^3\;+\;x\Big(C\,|v|^{1/3}+D\Big)
\]
with the *key* properties:

- **Has a pure \(v^3\) term** (odd in \(v\)): \(-0.02304\,v^3\).
- **Has an \(x|v|^{1/3}\) term** (non-polynomial fractional power, uses Abs): \(-1.1056\cdot 0.05524\,x|v|^{1/3}\).
- **Has a pure linear \(x\) term**: \(-2.2112\,x\).
- **Has a pure sinusoid in \(t\)**: \(+0.35078\sin t\).
- **No** tanh, no logs, no rational factors like \(1/(c+|v|)\), no \(x^3\), no constants, etc.

Also, because \(x,v\) can be negative, anything involving \(\tanh(\cdot)\), \(\log(\cdot)\), or \((c+|v|)^{-1}\) must be eliminated (set coefficients to 0) unless it can exactly reproduce the needed \(x|v|^{1/3}\) and \(x\) terms globally—which it cannot.

Now check candidates.

---

### Candidate 1
Contains: tanh(x), \(v^3\), cos(t+phase), \(x\log(1+k|v|)\), \(x^3\).
- We can set tanh term and \(x^3\) term to 0.
- Cos can match sin via phase shift.
- But GT needs \(x|v|^{1/3}\) and \(x\). Candidate has \(x\log(1+k|v|)\), which cannot equal \(a x|v|^{1/3}+bx\) for all \(v\) (log is not a fractional power + constant).
❌ No match.

### Candidates 2–20 (the “/(c2+Abs(v))” family)
All these have many terms multiplied by \(\frac{1}{c_2+|v|}\) and/or \(\frac{|v|}{c_2+|v|}\), plus tanh(x) factors, plus cos terms sometimes divided by \(c_2+|v|\), plus sometimes \(v^3|v|\) etc.
GT has **no such rational dependence on \(|v|\)**. To match GT globally, every term with denominator \((c_2+|v|)\) must vanish, because:
- \(\frac{1}{c_2+|v|}\), \(\frac{|v|}{c_2+|v|}\), \(\frac{v^3}{c_2+|v|}\), etc. are not polynomials nor \(|v|^{1/3}\), and cannot combine to produce exactly \(v^3\) plus \(|v|^{1/3}\) plus constants for all \(v\).
- Setting \(c_2=0\) makes them \(\sim 1/|v|\) or \(\sim v^3/|v|\), still wrong and singular at \(v=0\) (GT is finite at \(v=0\)).
So all denominator-terms must be zeroed by setting their coefficients to 0. After doing that, what remains in each candidate is checked:

- Many of 2–20 leave at best a standalone cos(t+phase) or constant or \(v^3\) or \(v^3|v|\). None can produce simultaneously:
  - \(x\) term and \(x|v|^{1/3}\) term (they have no free \(x\) outside tanh/log; tanh(x) is not linear in \(x\) globally).
  - and the correct \(v^3\) term.
Therefore each of 2–20 fails.

Concretely:
- Any remaining \(t\)-term is often scaled by \((c_2+|v|)^{-1}\) unless there is also an undivided cos term; but GT’s sinusoid is independent of \(v\).
- Any \(x\)-dependence is via \(\tanh(c_1 x)\), not linear \(x\).
- No candidate in 2–20 contains \(x|v|^{1/3}\) explicitly.

❌ Candidates 2–20: no match.

### Candidate 21
Like 1: tanh(x), \(v^3\), cos(t+phase), \(x\log(1+k|v|)\), \(x^3\).
Same obstruction: log cannot equal \(|v|^{1/3}\) + constant globally.
❌ No match.

### Candidate 22
Has denominator family plus undivided \(v^3|v|\) and undivided cos.
- Can set denominator terms to 0, keep cos (phase-shift to sin), but then left with \(v^3|v|\) which cannot equal \(v^3\) for negative \(v\) (it equals \(|v|^4\) with sign? actually \(v^3|v|=|v|^4\operatorname{sgn}(v)^3=|v|^4\operatorname{sgn}(v)\), not \(v^3\)).
- Still no linear \(x\) nor \(x|v|^{1/3}\).
❌ No match.

### Candidates 23–24, 27, 30, 40, 42–46, 49–50
These mix denominator terms with possibly an undivided \(v\) or \(v^3\) or cos.
- None introduce an \(x\) term except via \(\tanh(c_1 x)\), which cannot be made exactly proportional to \(x\) for all real \(x\) (only approximately near 0).
- None contain \(x|v|^{1/3}\) or anything that can be tuned to it.
- Any attempt to use \(\tanh(c_1 x)\) to represent \(x\) fails globally: \(\tanh\) saturates, \(x\) is unbounded.
❌ No match for all of these.

### Candidate 25
tanh(x), \(v^3\), cos(t+phase), \(x\log(1+k|v|)\), plus constant.
Still lacks \(x|v|^{1/3}\) and linear \(x\) (only via log term, which is wrong functional form).
❌ No match.

### Candidate 26
Has \(v^3\) (good) and cos(t+phase) (can phase shift), but \(x\)-dependence only through \(\tanh(c_1 x)/(c_2+|v|)\) etc. No linear \(x\), no \(x|v|^{1/3}\).
❌ No match.

### Candidate 28
Has \(v^3\), but \(t\)-term is divided by \((c_2+|v|)\) and \(x\)-terms absent except tanh/denominator. No way to get GT’s \(x\) and \(x|v|^{1/3}\).
❌ No match.

### Candidate 29
Like 21 but with extra \(+v^3\). Still uses \(x\log(1+k|v|)\) not \(x|v|^{1/3}\), and has tanh and \(x^3\).
❌ No match.

### Candidates 31, 33, 38
Contain \(v|v|/(c_2+|v|)\) etc. Still no linear \(x\) nor \(x|v|^{1/3}\); and denominator dependence cannot be removed while keeping needed terms.
❌ No match.

### Candidate 32
Even more complicated powers with denominators; no \(x\) linear or \(x|v|^{1/3}\).
❌ No match.

### Candidate 34
Like 1 but with an added constant. Same log vs \(|v|^{1/3}\) obstruction.
❌ No match.

### Candidate 35
Has \(v^3\) and denominator terms; no linear \(x\) or \(x|v|^{1/3}\).
❌ No match.

### Candidate 36
Has tanh(x), \(v^3\), cos(t+phase), \(x\log(1+k|v|)\), plus \(x\), constant, \(x^5\).
- We can set \(x^5\), tanh, constant to 0; keep \(x\) term (good), keep \(v^3\) (good), cos phase-shift (good).
- But still missing \(x|v|^{1/3}\); only available coupling is \(x\log(1+k|v|)\), which cannot equal \(x|v|^{1/3}\) globally.
❌ No match.

### Candidate 37
Has tanh(x), constant, \(v^3\), cos(t+phase), \(x\log(1+k|v|)\), and linear \(x\).
Same as 36: cannot generate \(x|v|^{1/3}\).
❌ No match.

### Candidate 39
Has tanh(x), linear \(x\), \(v^3\) (twice), cos(t+phase), \(x\log(1+k|v|)\), \(x^3\).
Again: cannot generate \(x|v|^{1/3}\).
❌ No match.

### Candidate 41
Has tanh(x), \(v^3\), cos(t+phase), \(x\log(1+k|v|)\), linear \(x\), constant.
Still lacks \(x|v|^{1/3}\).
❌ No match.

### Candidate 47
Adds an exp(t) term; can set it to 0, but still only has \(x\log(1+k|v|)\) not \(x|v|^{1/3}\).
❌ No match.

### Candidate 48
Denominator family; no linear \(x\) and no \(x|v|^{1/3}\).
❌ No match.

---

### Core reason none can match
Every candidate’s \(x\)-dependence is through **tanh(x)** and/or **\(x\log(1+k|v|)\)** and/or denominator factors \((c+|v|)^{-1}\). The GT requires an explicit **linear \(x\)** term plus an **\(x|v|^{1/3}\)** term. No candidate contains \(|v|^{1/3}\) or any function that can be tuned to exactly \(|v|^{1/3}\) for all real \(v\) (log and rational forms cannot be made identical to a fractional power globally). Therefore exact equivalence is impossible.

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match

GT Equivalence Verification (PO4)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - omega0**c1*(gamma*Abs(v)**c2 + c3)*x - omega0**c4*x
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to analyze whether each candidate can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.0230405*v³ - 1.10561*x*(0.05524*|v|^(1/3) + 1) - 1.10561*x + 0.35078*sin(t)`

Simplifying GT:
`-0.0230405*v³ - 1.10561*0.05524*x*|v|^(1/3) - 1.10561*x - 1.10561*x + 0.35078*sin(t)`
`= -0.0230405*v³ - 0.06108*x*|v|^(1/3) - 2.21121*x + 0.35078*sin(t)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `v³` 
2. `x*|v|^(1/3)` 
3. `x` (linear)
4. `sin(t)` (equivalently `cos(t + phase)`)

Key structural features:
- **`x*|v|^(1/3)`**: This is a critical term - x multiplied by a fractional power of |v|
- **Linear in x**: The x terms are linear (not tanh(x) or other nonlinear functions)

Now let me examine the candidates. Most candidates use `tanh(c1*x)` instead of `x`. The function `tanh(c1*x)` is NOT equivalent to a linear function `c*x` for all x values. Since x takes both positive and negative values in the PO4 domain, and the domain likely includes values where tanh saturates, `tanh(c1*x) ≠ c*x` in general.

However, if `c1` can be set arbitrarily close to 0, then `tanh(c1*x) ≈ c1*x` for small `c1*x`. But this is an approximation, not exact equivalence. Per Rule 2, approximations are forbidden.

**Candidates 1, 21, 25, 29, 34, 36, 37, 39, 41, 47**: These use `tanh(c1*x)` and `x*log(c*|v|+1)`. Note that `log(c*|v|+1)` is NOT equivalent to `|v|^(1/3)` for any constant choice. Also `tanh(c1*x)` ≠ linear in x. These are **NO MATCH**.

**Candidates 2-20, 22-28, 30-33, 35, 38, 40, 42-50**: These all use `tanh(c1*x)` as the x-dependent function. Since `tanh(c1*x)` cannot exactly equal a linear function `a*x` for all x, and the GT requires linear x terms, none of these can match.

Additionally, many candidates use rational functions of `|v|` like `v³/(c2+|v|)` and `v³*|v|/(c2+|v|)`. Note that `v³*|v|/(c2+|v|) + v³/(c2+|v|) = v³*(|v|+1)/(c2+|v|)` which equals `v³` only if `c2=1`, but even combining all v³-related terms, we'd need to reproduce `v³` and `x*|v|^(1/3)` exactly. The `|v|^(1/3)` term cannot be produced from rational functions of `|v|`.

Even if we could somehow handle the `tanh` issue (which we can't), the `x*|v|^(1/3)` term requires a fractional power that none of the rational-in-|v| candidates can produce.

Let me verify: Can `tanh(c1*x)` with `c1→0` work? No, Rule 2 forbids approximations.

**Candidate 48** uses `tanh(c1*x)` without the `/(c2+|v|)` factor on the first term, but still has the same fundamental issues.

All candidates fail because:
1. They use `tanh(c1*x)` instead of linear `x`
2. They cannot produce `x*|v|^(1/3)` from their basis functions
